





CATALOGUE
OF A VERY EXTENSIVE
COLLECTION OF PRINTS,
By Ancient and Modern Masters,
DIVIDED INTO TWO PARTS.
PART I.
CONTAINING A SERIES OF ENGRAVED BRITISH PORTRAITS,
Commencing with the Reign of EGBERT, and continued to the present Time,
CONSISTING OF
MORE THAN FIVE THOUSAND DIFFERENT PRINTS;
AMONG WHICH ARE MANY VERY SCARCE BY
DELARAM, ELSTRACKE, FAITHORNE, GLOVER,
HOLLAR, LOGGAN, MARSHALL, PASS,
SMITH, VANDREBANC VERTUE, WHITE, &c.
FINE PROOFS AFTER SIR JOSHUA,
And a numerous APPENDIX of upwards of ONE THOUSAND PORTRAITS of FOREIGNERS
belonging to the English Series.
PART II.
COMBINING THE CAPITAL PRODUCTIONS OF THE MOST CELEBRATED ARTISTS
OF THE
German, Dutch, Flemish, French, and English Schools,
FROM THE EARLIEST ÆRA OF THE ARTS TO THE PRESENT PERIOD;
SEVERAL APPROACHING TO ALMOST ENTIRE WORKS OF THE MASTER, AND ARE OF
THE CHOICEST IMPRESSION, AS WELL AS IN HIGH PRESERVATION.
THE WHOLE EXHIBITING
THE LARGEST ASSEMBLAGE OF VALUABLE PRINTS
HITHERTO OFFERED TO THE PUBLIC,
And collected with great Care and Expence for several Years past from the Cabinets of
BARNARD, ROGERS, WOODHOUSE, MUSGRAVE, LAKE, TIGHE, TYSSEN, WALDRON,
AND OTHERS OF A MORE RECENT DATE.
Now adjusted for Sale, at the Prices mentioned in the Catalogue, without any Abatement, by
ROBERT GRAVE,
(SON OF THE LATE MR. ROBERT GRAVE)
At No. 239, TOTTENHAM COURT ROAD, near BEDFORD STREET,
Where Catalogues may be had, at 7s. each.
Printed by J, & W. Smith, King Street, Seven Dials.




FROM the increasing demand that has been made of late for Portraits,
of every description, for the purpose of illustrating various celebrated
Works, and in consequence of great numbers having been locked up for
ever from the possession of individuals, occasioned by the numerous bequests
of many rich collections to different publick institutions, insomuch that
many portraits, which a few years since were thought common, and easily
to be met with, are now become comparatively scarce, and in all probability
in a short time, will, with difficulty be procured. The proprietor submits
the following Catalogue to the attention of the Nobility and Gentry, who
now have an opportunity of obtaining portraits of their ancestors, or of
materially adding to their own collections.
With respect to the numerous works which compose the second pari
of this catalogue j as there are many selections that constitute by far the
greater portion of the several masters, and others that require very fexo to
render them complete; the proprietor respectfully informs the admirers of
the graphic art, that as it xoould be attended with regret to break them up
after the great pains and length of time expended in their accumulation,,
it is rather his object to dispose of them collectively, or else in detached
works, than otherwise; and in that case, should any Nobleman or Gentleman
feel inclined to possess them, a liberal abatement will be made in proportion
to the amount purchased.
R. GRAVE,
July 15, 1809.

Foreigners belonging to the English Series.
j\N- EXTENSIVE COLLECTION OF PORTRAITS OF SUCH FOREIGNERS
BELONGING TO THE ENGLISH SERIES, as have been Naturalized, pos-
sessed any Dignity, held any Employment, or who may have visited or
resided in this Country; comprising Granger’s and Bromley’s Appendixes,
BUT ENLARGED TO A CONSIDERABLE DEGREE, AND CONSISTING OF UPWARDS OF
ONE THOUSAND DIFFERENT PORTRAITS, among which are a Number
NOT GENERALLY KNOWN, AND MANY VERY RARE AND CURIOUS —THE WHOLE
FORMED WITH GREAT LABOUR AND ATTENTION DURING A PERIOD OF MORE THAN
Thirty Years.
